Record of the Great Academic Exploration of Manchuria and Mongolia (2) (Translated from Osaka Asahi Shimbun) 89

According to Takeshi Nakai, Director of the Botanical Garden of Tokyo University and Doctor of Science, regarding the plants of Jehol Province, in terms of our current level of knowledge, our minds are almost blank. No one has ever investigated plants in that region. However, there is some discussion in the research papers of French botanists, but these are also old works. Considering the progress of learning today, there are many points that should be corrected. I recall that twenty years ago, the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce secretly investigated the forests of the hunting grounds, but the obtained data was unfortunately burned during the Great Earthquake, so the truth of the investigation results at that time is also unknown. In 1864 AD, the French missionary David (A. David) went to Chengde in Jehol Province, collected some plants from the vicinity, and collected countless specimens in northern, central China, Mongolia, and eastern Siberia, sending them to Professor E. Bureau of the National Museum of Paris, France. At that time, Professor Bureau served as the assistant of A. Francbet, a famous plant taxonomist at the museum. He studied the sent specimens one by one, and as a result, he titled the plants obtained from China as "Plantae Davdianae ex Sinarum lmperio" and published it to the world.

The first part, volumes 5 to 7 of the "Memoirs of the Paris Museum, Series 2," was published in 1884 and recorded plants from northern and central China, Mongolia, Jehol, etc. The second part, volumes 8 to 10 of the Memoirs, was published in 1888 and recorded plants from eastern Tibet. The first part, on the plants of Jehol Province, includes 398 species, of which 15 are ferns, 80 are monocotyledons, 303 are dicotyledons, 42 are shrubs, and 26 are trees. Among these new plants, 13 new species, 17 new varieties, and 4 unusual species were unknown to the academic community at that time. However, David's collection area was only in the vicinity of Chengde. Based on our past experience, if we meticulously investigate and study the plants collected from even just one mountain range in East Asia, we can discover at least 50 new plants unknown to the academic community. Moreover, the area of Jehol to be investigated this time is very vast, including large mountains, hills, deserts, rivers, and wetlands, making it the most complex terrain in Manchuria. Therefore, future great discoveries in the field of plant taxonomy will be countless.

Regarding animals, according to Hisayoshi Kishida, entrusted by the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry, in the first half of the eighth century, during the reign of Emperor Shōmu of Japan, an envoy from the Balhae Kingdom named Mong Ijin crossed over to Japan, presenting six pelts each of Manchurian tigers, red bears, and clouded leopards, three shih of honey, and countless other rare birds and animals. According to the animal catalogues of Tokumasu in 1909, Kiyonosuke Uchida in 1915, Tamemori Mori in 1922, and Shasaizhai in 1923, the same animals produced in Manchuria have similar variants in Jehol. In addition, some animals that thrive in the large deserts of the northern temperate zone of Asia, from Mongolia to Turkestan, also breed in Jehol. There are also animals similar to those in northern China, southern Manchuria, and the main part of Korea, as well as animals similar to those in northern Manchuria, northern Korea, and Sakhalin, as well as mixed desert species, all of which are included in the collection plan.

Regarding anthropological research, according to Ichiro Yawatā, entrusted by the East, it is speculated that traces of human ancestors can be found in the Jehol region. Manchuria and Mongolia are vast areas for anthropological activity. We should first investigate the current Manchus, Mongolians, and other Siberian peoples living along the Songhua River and Heilongjiang River, as well as their ethnological situation. This kind of investigation is very important because their physical characteristics and culture are gradually changing from their old state, and no one knows what their inherent characteristics are. On the other hand, there are many issues in the study of ancient humans that can be clarified in cooperation with paleontology and archaeology. In particular, there is a great need for anthropological explanation and research on the rise and fall of the Manchurian and Mongolian peoples and the origins of their current migrations. Therefore, the ethnic history of this region can provide powerful materials for cultural history. The area to be investigated and studied this time is spearheaded by the Dr. Torii couple, because the couple has been investigating in this area since the 40th year of Meiji, experiencing various hardships. They have discovered many remains from the Neolithic Age onwards, such as the remains, tools, and utensils of primitive humans, but no Paleolithic remains have been found there to date. It is said that traces of the ancestors of mankind can be found between Zhoukoudian, Hejiagou, and Zhalainuoer. In addition, since the Neolithic Age, the area of contention between the Han Chinese and the northern peoples is particularly worthy of our attention and research.

Chiang and Wang's Telegram Instructs Ping on Ways to Deal with Chahar 90

Assess the Situation and Seek a Solution. 50,000 Troops Enter Chahar. Bandit Troops Plot to Invade Duolun.

Special Dispatch from Beiping: Since the peaceful negotiation of the Chahar incident came to a standstill, the Beiping authorities have been quietly awaiting the determination of the policy at the Lushan Conference before seeking to proceed. The Lushan Conference has already discussed ways to deal with the Chahar incident. Last night, Chiang and Wang sent a telegram to Ping instructing everything, divided into two steps. The first step is to first use letters and telegrams or send senior officials to Chahar again to earnestly negotiate and be frank with each other in order to resolve the matter as soon as possible. The second step is to take effective measures based on the actual situation to seek a thorough solution. The Ping authorities immediately proceeded according to the instructions in the telegram. Yesterday, He Yingqin invited Xiong Bin to the Jurenhan Hall to discuss matters. This morning (27th, Xiong Bin), Liu Zhilong, Jia Deyao, and others visited Song Zheyuan at the Wuyiku, hoping that Song would make further efforts to mediate. Song did not express a firm opinion due to his difficult situation and lingering back pain. However, he said that Feng was his former superior and that, at a time when the country was in such a difficult situation, he hoped for a peaceful resolution for both public and private reasons. After Gong Bingxun's troops made slight changes, the forward defense area was taken over by Wang Jingjiu's 87th Division. Weng Zhaoyuan's division of Wang Yizhe's troops also moved to Kangzhuang. Guan Linzheng's division has moved one step forward. Feng Qinzai's troops are stationed near Linlai. Pang Xun's troops are responsible for the line between Shacheng and Zhuolu. The area north of Shacheng is entirely garrisoned by the Central Army. The two sides are separated by Xinzhuangzi. It is said that the various armies were ordered to enter Chahar, first to garrison, second to make necessary preparations, and third to take precautions because the garrison in Chahar Province is complex.

At the beginning of the recapture of Duolun, it was guarded by the troops of Ji Hongchang and Zhang Lingyun to search for the remnants of the enemy and to pacify the area. Recently, Ji's troops were ordered to be transferred back to Zhangbei and the vicinity of Zhangjiakou to garrison. Only Zhang Lingyun's troops were left to guard Duolun. Liu Guitang's troops were stationed in the area of Guyuan, south of Duolun. Li Zhongyi and Deng Wen's troops are stationed in the areas of Saichang and Kangbao. The Japanese and puppet troops consider Duolun and Guyuan as important border areas of the puppet state and cannot forget them. At first, they actively mobilized troops and prepared to counterattack. Recently, the Japanese army claimed to have stopped advancing, while the puppet army, seeing that Ji's troops had withdrawn from the Duolun area and the defense was weak, plotted to invade again. The troops of Cui Xingwu and Zhang Haipeng have a tendency to advance towards Duolun and Guyuan. If the Chahar incident is not resolved soon, the eastern part of Chahar may ultimately be uneasy. Thereupon, Xue Zhiheng, Lei Shourong, Li Zeyi, and others worked hard on the reorganization of Li's troops. After several negotiations, a considerable decision was finally reached. The amount of all expenses was 348,000 yuan as rumored in Pingjin and 484,000 yuan as rumored in Tangshan. We outsiders have yet to understand. Since the reorganization issue has been properly settled, the method of receiving administrative power has also been changed, and it has been decided to proceed from difficult to easy. Song Naigan was ordered to go to Tangshan on the 22nd to receive the Public Security Bureau. Song and Li have a historical origin in the military world (during Li Jinglin's governorship of Zhili, Li Jichun was the commander of the 7th Division, and Song Naigan was the brigade commander in the 7th Division). The reception seems to be easier, but it was delayed until the 24th before it could be received. At the time of the change of power, Li actually sent a representative, Zhang Shouxian, to deliver a speech in the name of the Chairman of the Reorganization Committee. After the reception of Tangshan, the Receiving Committee immediately decided on the receiving steps and set off in two routes, northeast and south. Those belonging to the northern route, the county magistrates and public security chiefs of Miyun, Zunhua, Jixian, Huairou, and Pinggu, gathered in Beiping on the 24th and were led by Receiving Commissioner Tao Shangming to Ningyun on the 25th to contact the commander of the Suzuki Brigade before heading to receive the area in different routes. Those belonging to the eastern route, the county magistrates and public security chiefs of Ninghe, Yutian, Fengrun, Luanxian, Leting, Qian'an, Lulong, Funing, Changli, and Linyu, were also scheduled to go to Tangshan on the 24th, and the Receiving Committee prepared a letter of introduction to contact Li Jichun. At the same time, they urged the provincial government to quickly organize two detachments (4,600 men) of the War Zone Security Team and assign them to various counties to accompany the county magistrates to receive the area. However, Provincial Chairman Yu Xuezhong believes that the reception of political power focuses on substance rather than form. If the reception can be done smoothly, then not a single soldier is needed. If there are disputes, even if an armed security team is brought along, the reception cannot be forcibly carried out. Even if the reception is forcibly carried out, the political power cannot be exercised in the future. However, the Receiving Committee has already passed this resolution, so it is not convenient to deny it. Therefore, it was decided to first establish one detachment, appointing Xi Zhezhe (Zi Guangdian) as the detachment commander, with a total of more than 1,800 men, with one company stationed in each county, and the detachment headquarters located in Tangshan. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 26th, a telegram suddenly came from Tangshan, stating that "Li's troops are to be reorganized locally and cannot be concentrated at the designated locations (i.e., Fengrun and Luanxian). Receiving personnel in various counties, please do not bring too many security teams other than the security team for personal protection to avoid misunderstandings. The situation in Qian'an County is complicated and there are many bandits. The Japanese troops in the county have not been ordered to withdraw and refuse to receive the area. Please postpone the trip of the county magistrate of the county, Lu Qingchen, for the time being." After Receiving Commissioner Yin Tong received the telegram, he went to see Chairman Yu to explain everything. Yu was deeply suspicious and said that since there were still so many twists and turns, it would be best to postpone the reception until Li's troops were concentrated at the designated locations and all obstacles in the various counties were completely cleared before proceeding with the reception. Yin said that the reception was no longer a problem and that it was only to prevent any misunderstandings that the departing personnel were ordered to bring fewer security teams. Currently, only Qian'an could not be received and that continued negotiations would be held. After consultation, it was decided that the county magistrates would still depart according to the scheduled time limit, with only four companies of security teams temporarily dispatched, a total of 608 men, led by the detachment commander Dou Xizhe, with two companies stationed in Linyu County and one company each in Fengrun and Luanxian Counties. Yin Tong was deeply afraid that Chairman Yu would not order the receiving personnel to depart at the appointed time, so he went to Beiping by special train at 2:00 p.m. on the 26th to report to Huang Fu. At 6:00 p.m., Huang immediately ordered the provincial government by long-distance telephone to send personnel to depart and receive the area according to the scheduled steps. Receiving personnel in each county were only allowed to carry a small number of guards, and the rest of the security teams that had already been formed were to postpone their departure. Therefore, at 3:30 a.m. and 4:30 a.m. today (27th), two special trains departed from the East Station, with only two companies of security teams, fully armed, and with several machine guns attached, to protect the departing receiving personnel. According to Yu Shengxi, "Fengrun County Magistrate Zhang Renli went to Tangshan on the 24th to make contact and has not yet returned to Tianjin. Yesterday morning (26th), Li sent personnel to accompany him to receive the area, so there should be no problem. The reception of Qian'an has been postponed, and it is said that the situation is complicated, but I do not know exactly how complicated it is. Japanese soldiers at the major stations from Tangshan to Yuguan are reportedly temporarily refusing to withdraw on the pretext of the Boxer Protocol, which violates the spirit of the Tanggu Agreement. Further negotiations will be needed in the future. There are 6,000 to 7,000 soldiers of the Japanese army's Hattori Brigade stationed in Yuguan, and there is no news of their withdrawal. In my opinion, they may again use the excuse of being the puppet state's security force. The situation in Linyu is also very complicated. Although Receiving Commissioner Liu Shisun has sent a telegram reporting that there are no problems, there are a large number of Japanese and Korean ronin there, so the negotiations in the future cannot be underestimated. Therefore, Liu Shaokun, the secretary of the provincial capital's public security bureau, has also been additionally assigned to accompany the county magistrate Yin Shousong on his departure. The Japanese army's sentry line in Yuguan is in the Shihe area, which is what the Japanese side considers to be the puppet state's security line. It is also reported that the puppet state has been working hard to appease bandits in various places outside the customs and secretly transporting them into the customs. Recently, many bandits have been lurking in the Chaoyangdong, Jiaoshan, Shimen, and Yiyuan Pass areas north of Linyu County. In the future, it will be very difficult for us to suppress them, and they may flee in our direction. The provincial government has remitted 25,000 yuan for Li Jichun's troops' food and supplies for July, and they have recently demanded their salaries for July (said to be 48,000 yuan), which I have rejected. Regarding the salaries of the troops, they must wait until the reorganization is completed and the provincial government sends personnel to verify the number before they can be officially paid. Li's request for 8,000 yuan per month for the expenses of the Chairman's Office of the Reorganization Committee must also be approved by the standing committee of the provincial government before it can be determined. In addition, it is said that 6,000 of Li's troops who are surplus after the reorganization will be transported by the Beining Railway Bureau to Machang on the Jinpu Railway for dissolution. Most of the troops are from outside the customs and are bandits and vagrants from outside the customs. Now, instead of being transported outside the customs for dissolution, they are being transported to Machang in Hebei Province for dissolution. These people have nowhere to go and will inevitably become bandits in the future. The war-torn Ji Province will have these thousands of unemployed vagrants, and the local security is a cause for concern." The first train of 1,200 of Li's surplus troops arrived at Machang at 12:00 last night and were not allowed to disembark. The matter has been reported to the Military Affairs Commission in Beiping for instructions on resettlement measures. (July 27)

Zheng Guilin's Troops Mutiny 93

Zheng's Troops Have Poor Discipline

Heard That They Will Go to Chahar After the Mutiny

Special Dispatch from Tianjin: Zheng Guilin gained a good reputation last year for resisting Japan outside the customs, but the elements of his troops were bad and their discipline was poor. However, because he raised the banner of resistance against Japan, everyone concealed his misdeeds. This year, when Rehe Province fell, Zheng also led his troops into the customs after many twists and turns. The Beiping Military Affairs Commission gave him a monthly maintenance fee of 20,000 yuan and assigned him to the command of He Guozhu. In reality, He was also unable to control him. This summer, when Tangshan fell, Zheng's troops retreated to the territory of Ninghe County, where they committed kidnapping, extortion, rape, arson, and murder, committing all kinds of evil. The dozens of villages, large and small, within 50 to 60 li around them were reduced to scorched earth. The degree of suffering cannot be described in words. At that time, the local gentry repeatedly appealed for the disarming of the troops, and Yu Xuezhong consulted He Zhuguo's opinion. He said that the Military Affairs Commission was still tolerant and gave them 20,000 yuan per month, so why should we play the role of an evil person? Later, the Military Affairs Commission gave Zheng the nominal title of Provisional First Division Commander and sent him to Machang for training. Unexpectedly, he did not change his wild nature. After arriving at Machang, he still went out to cause trouble and was not subject to restraint. Zheng was still not satisfied and appointed a certain person as the Second Division Commander and recruited troops in Anci and other counties. The matter was learned by the First Army Corps and they were ordered to disband. Last week, Zheng's troops stationed at Machang mutinied twice, with 500 to 600 people looting the station and seriously injuring the stationmaster. Finally, Zheng was held hostage by his subordinates and the entire unit mutinied and fled. They first captured Renqiu County and extorted tens of thousands of yuan. It is said that they will flee to Chahar Province. The troops still have more than 2,000 men. After passing through Hejian, Lixian, Suning, and other counties, all villages and towns were looted, and the guns of the militias and police were confiscated. The local losses were extremely heavy. In addition to sending two battalions of infantry from the 114th Division of the First Army Corps and two companies of cavalry from Zhang Chengde to pursue and suppress the troops, the First Army Corps also telegraphed the garrisons in various counties to encircle and suppress them strictly. It is expected that they will be put down soon. (July 27)

The Jiangxi Bandits Invade Xunwu Again 94

Scattered by Five Routes of Encirclement and Suppression by Various Armies

The Bandits Invading Shibanwei Also Suffered Heavy Losses

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since the Southern Route bandit suppression army arrived in Xunwu, Anyuan, and other places, it has been actively deployed and advanced. Unexpectedly, taking advantage of the fact that the official army's forward deployment was not prepared, the communist bandits suddenly gathered 5,000 to 6,000 people from Ruijin and Huichang on the 16th of this month and launched a fierce attack on Xunwu. The Xunwu garrison's 8th Division's battalions of Ouyang Xin and Chen Fengshao fought fiercely separately, holding their ground for a day and night. The 7th Division of the Southern Route Army immediately rushed to their aid, while the Independent 1st Division and the 4th Division of Southern Jiangxi also separately outflanked the bandit positions. After a day and night of bloody fighting with five routes encircling the bandits, the bandits were defeated and scattered towards Peixi and Gaopai, north of Xunwu, gathering in the Junmenling area. The Southern Route Army has now ordered the aircraft units on the northeast routes to take off and reconnoiter and bomb the bandit areas. Ao Lun, the deputy captain of the 5th Air Unit in Meixian, Eastern Guangdong, has already led four aircraft to take off and take on the task of bombing the bandit areas of Junmen and Huichang. Tao Zuode, the captain of the 3rd Air Unit in Northern Guangdong, also led two aircraft from Shaozhou on the 20th and moved to Longnan to take on the task of reconnoitering and bombing the bandit nests near Anyuan. On the 18th, the defense area of the Yan Brigade of the Independent 1st Division was again invaded by more than 700 bandits, who split into groups to disturb the Luoxuan military line of our army. The brigade immediately dispatched three artillery companies to suppress the bandits. After about five hours of fighting, the bandits increased their reinforcements by more than 300 and advanced to Changgengwei, disturbing the rear of the brigade. Brigade Commander Yan again dispatched Chen Shuyau's battalion to attack. The bandits' plan failed and they gradually retreated towards Chishaling, killing more than 400 bandits along the way, capturing a communist bandit daredevil captain Yuan Guangzu and more than a dozen male and female bandits, and seizing 20 local rifles and one local cannon. At present, the 2nd Column of Eastern Jiangxi is preparing considerable forces for defense because the military situation in Junmen and Xunwu is still tense. The 1st Column has also engaged in fighting in Anyuan and Southern Jiangxi in recent days while searching for remnants of the communists. On the 10th of this month, a bloody battle occurred in Shibanwei near Anyuan, in which Chen Jing's troops of the 12th Regiment of the 4th Division engaged in hand-to-hand combat eight times with more than 4,000 bandits, and in the final counterattack, more than 1,000 bandits were killed or wounded, leaving behind more than 400 corpses. The official army suffered casualties of six platoon leaders and more than 30 soldiers. On the 17th of this month, the 4th Division dispatched Kong Kequan's battalion of the 10th Regiment to advance towards Longbu and encountered the communist bandit pseudo-Red Guard 12th Regiment in Tianxinwei. They fought for one night, and Huang Zhenbiao, the 10th company commander of the Kong Battalion, led his troops to be the first to break through the bandit positions, and the bandit troops retreated in disarray towards Huichang. The 10th Regiment entered Tianxinwei on the same day. The division has promoted Huang, the company commander, to the third battalion commander of the 10th Regiment in recognition of his bravery in killing the enemy in this battle.

On the 12th, Li Chonggang's battalion of the 5th Regiment of the 2nd Division of the 1st Army south of Ganzhou searched the Meirenkeng and Zhongcun areas from Huangni Pai and encircled a bandit gang of about 20 or 30 local communists. After the encirclement and suppression, they captured a communist bandit named Huang in the forest and seized a red flag of the Xinfeng Guerrilla Company of the Chinese Soviet. On the 14th, more than 400 Red Army soldiers of the 24th Division were found in Xintianwei. Ye Gengchang's regiment of the 2nd Division, stationed in Gupo, dispatched a company to suppress them on the 15th. The bandits stubbornly resisted from the high ground of Xintianwei and relied on solid fortifications. They engaged in a fierce battle with the official army on the 16th for several hours. The bandits were defeated only after the official army destroyed the bandit bunkers with artillery fire. More than 30 bandits were killed and several guns were seized. (July 24)

Regulations for Opium Prohibition in Guangxi Province 95

Those Who Use Opium Are Required to Quit in Three Stages

Opium Dens Prohibited Starting in October

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangxi’s Kunlian and Qianwen Yingli areas are convenient for transportation, so many Guangxi people use opium. Recently, the Guangxi Provincial Government, recognizing the increasing harm of opium, designated special opium and gambling zones in various counties. Areas outside these special zones are strictly prohibited. Recently, the Provincial Government announced regulations for opium prohibition throughout the province, instructing all counties to implement them. The regulations are as follows: (1) Opium prohibition in Guangxi Province, except where otherwise stipulated by criminal law and special laws, shall be handled in accordance with the provisions of these regulations. (2) In areas with Public Security Bureaus, the prohibition of opium shall be the responsibility of the Public Security Bureau. In areas without Public Security Bureaus, it shall be the responsibility of the county government. (3) Each county government or Public Security Bureau shall be responsible for supervising its subordinate district, township, village, street, and neighborhood leaders to determine the number of opium users within its jurisdiction within one and a half months from July 1, 1933, and to compile a detailed list for reporting to the Provincial Government for review. The form for this list will be determined separately. (4) If the district, township, village, street, and neighborhood leaders conduct inaccurate investigations or arbitrarily fill out reports, they will be investigated and punished by the county magistrate or Public Security Bureau chief upon discovery. (5) Each county government or Public Security Bureau lecture hall should print flyers in simple language, send personnel to various streets and villages to promote and persuade, and instruct each school to organize lecture teams during holidays to go out and give lectures, so that the people deeply understand the harm of opium use and are determined to quit. (6) All opium users, regardless of gender or age, must quit by the end of July 1933. Those who cannot quit after three months must obtain a monthly opium use license and pay a license fee to be allowed to use opium. The license form will be determined and issued separately. (7) Opium users obtaining an opium use license shall pay the license fee in three-month installments. The first installment is one yuan per month, the second installment is two yuan per month, and the third installment is four yuan per month. If, after the third installment, they have not yet quit or use opium privately without a license, they will be punished according to law. (8) Those over 60 years of age or who use opium due to illness, as certified by a doctor, may obtain an opium use license and report to the Provincial Government for record on a monthly basis. (10) Opium users who are able to quit during the prohibition period must have two or more neighborhood leaders from their village or street issue a certificate stating that they will never use opium again, and submit it to the county government or Public Security Bureau for compilation and monthly submission to the Provincial Government for record. (11) Opium users who have quit may still be inspected at any time if necessary. (12) All opium dens in the cities and counties shall be prohibited from opening, starting from October 1, 1934. (July 23rd)

Resolutions of the Jiaoji Railway Council on the Method of Redeeming the Railway 96

Allocate Annual Savings to Form a Railway Redemption Fund

Raise Domestic Public Bonds to Cover the Shortfall

Qingdao Correspondence: The Jiaoji Railway Council held a meeting in the railway conference hall at 10:00 AM on July 24th. The attendees included Chairman Wang Zhengting, Councilors Yan Deqing, Ge Guangting, Chen Yanwen, and Council Secretary Zhao Cisheng. Chairman Wang Zhengting presided, and Zhao Citseng recorded the minutes. The meeting proceeded as planned, with the following items: Reporting Items: (omitted) Discussion Items: (1) Proposal to allocate the railway's annual savings to establish a railway redemption fund. (Explanation) The railway currently owes the national treasury 40 million Japanese yen in bonds. With less than five years remaining until the prescribed repayment deadline, it is appropriate to make arrangements as soon as possible to uphold national credit. After careful review of the railway's economic situation and revenue and expenditure status, it is proposed to raise 2 million Japanese yen annually starting in 1933. Within five years, the railway can repay at least 10 million yen of the bond principal. The remaining shortfall will be covered by raising domestic public bonds or seeking loans from domestic banking syndicates to settle the debt. Whether this is appropriate is respectfully submitted for public resolution. Resolution: Passed in principle, to be submitted to the ministry for record. (2) Proposal to gradually complete the replacement of the 85-pound steel rails east of Zhangdian Station. (Explanation) The railway previously used British Boxer Indemnity funds to purchase 85-pound steel rails to replace the light rails from Chengyang west to the Dawei River. This work is nearing completion. However, the railway's heavy-load cars all originate from Zhangdian. The section from the Dawei River to Zhangdian should also be replaced with heavy rails to increase speed and improve driving efficiency. The remaining funds from the railway's British Boxer Indemnity loan are sufficient to handle this project. It is proposed to replace them in stages. It is respectfully submitted for public resolution. Resolution: Passed. (3) Proposal to pilot the improvement of agricultural and forestry industries along the railway line to expand production. (Explanation) The land along the railway line is fertile and rich in resources. However, due to the people's lack of scientific knowledge, they tend to adhere to ancient methods for various production industries, with little improvement. Railways in Western countries often provide guidance and equipment for production industries along their lines, which benefits both parties. The railway intends to follow this example and plans to request several plots of wasteland from the Shandong Provincial Department of Construction to be used as forest farms, promoting afforestation. It also plans to subsidize Qilu University with a certain amount of funds each month, requesting its specialized professors to lead students in studying the points that should be improved in the agricultural products along the railway line for guidance. Whether this is appropriate is respectfully submitted for public resolution. Resolution: Passed in principle, to be handled by the railway bureau itself by formulating concrete measures. (July 27th)

Sudden Rise in the Si River in Shandong 97

Sharp Rise in the Upper Reaches of the Yellow River

Jinan Correspondence: Continuous rainy weather in southern Shandong has caused mountain torrents and a sharp rise in the water level of various rivers. The Si River has risen sharply by 2.78 meters. The East Si River has already exceeded its highest water level and is still rising. Therefore, not only is the East Si River, which is under construction and dredging, affected, causing delays in the work, but the sharp rise in water may also lead to flooding disasters. After receiving a report from the Si River supervisor Zhao Dongsheng from Jining yesterday, the Department of Construction has telegraphed each county along the Si River to strictly prevent flooding disasters.

The upper, middle, and lower reaches of the Yellow River have risen by 5-6 centimeters in recent days. The water source in the upper reaches is very strong and unusually abundant. According to a telegram received by the provincial government from Shaanxi Chairman Shao Lizhi on the 20th, as reported by Pingmin County Magistrate Mao Hanwen, the Yellow River has risen, and on the 10th, the Fengjia Village north of Yongji County in Shanxi Province was breached. The floodwaters flowed south, directly impacting the west gate of Pingmin County, destroying more than twenty dams. The area between the east gate of Yongji County and the west gate of Pingmin County became a flooded area, and all the crops were submerged. The provincial government believes that the Yellow River has risen very high this year. Now that it has breached in Shanxi, Shandong, located in the lower reaches, should also take practical precautions. It has ordered the River Affairs Bureau to be strictly vigilant about the rise in water in the upper reaches. The River Affairs Bureau has notified all its officers and soldiers. Today (26th),

The water level at Dongzhuang in the upper reaches of the Yellow River has risen by 2.3 centimeters, with a water level of 58.15 meters. The water level at Luokou in the middle reaches has risen by 0.3 centimeters, with a water level of 29.86 meters. The water level at Damajia in the lower reaches has risen by 0.16 centimeters, with a water level of 14.32 meters. The water level is still rising. (26th)

experienced disputes. After more than a month of stalemate, the situation has become deadlocked. On the morning of the 27th, the Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau reported that the Qingjiangpu main gate was at 2 zhang due to the rapid rise in the Huai River. If it continues to rise, the lives and property of the residents along the canal will be at risk. Fortunately, the water level in the Jiangdu section is still stable, with the San Gou Gate measuring 1.11 zhang. The Gaobao section reported that the Yuma dedication water level has only risen by 1 cun, so the downstream panic is less severe than in the upstream.

Dai Ji Speaks After Returning to Shanghai Yesterday Morning 116

The Garrison Headquarters Will Not Be Abolished

The Successor Has Not Been Determined, Temporarily Handled by Zhang Xiang

After Relinquishing His Position, Dai Plans to Travel to North China

Songhu Garrison Commander Dai Ji was recently ordered by the Central Government to serve as a member of the Fujian Provincial Government and concurrently as the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs. After receiving the order, Dai went to Gan to pay respects to Chairman Chiang in order to personally inquire about everything. He completed his official duties on the morning of the day before (27th) and took a boat to Nanjing. After landing in Nanjing, he immediately changed to the Shanghai-Nanjing express train that afternoon and returned to the North Station at 0:30 yesterday morning. Yesterday morning, the reporter visited Dai at the Garrison Headquarters, inquired about the process of meeting with Chiang, the issue of the existence of the Garrison Headquarters, and when he would go to Fujian to take office. He replied as follows:

Meeting with Chiang 117

Dai said, "I had previously submitted my resignation to the Central Government

repeatedly, but it was not approved. Later, I received a telegram from Chairman Chiang summoning me, so I went to Nanchang a few days ago to pay my respects and inquire about everything. When I arrived in Nanchang, Chairman Chiang had just left for Guling, so I changed my route to Lu to pay my respects. I was instructed by Chairman Chiang to go to Fujian as soon as possible. When I paid my respects, Chairman Chiang was very busy, so the time for our talk was very short. Regarding the

Existence of the Garrison Headquarters 118

issue, there was no mention. However, I believe that Shanghai is an important area for national defense, and the Garrison Headquarters is still necessary. I have not heard of the rumors that it will be abolished.

Successor 119

Regarding the successor to the Songhu Garrison Commander, it has not yet been decided. When I met with Chairman Chiang, I asked who would succeed me. Chairman Chiang said that no one has been appointed yet. Before the successor is announced, all the duties of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters will be temporarily handled by the Chief of Staff of the department, Zhang Xiang. It is expected that the successor will be officially announced soon. I am now instructing the staff of this department to expedite the handover procedures so that I can relinquish my position when the successor is announced.

Planning to Travel to North China 120

After leaving school in 1915, I joined the army and have had no time to rest. I have not been to various places in North China for more than ten years. Now, I plan to take some time to travel to various places in North China after the handover here and when the January 28th Memorial Hall is completed, and then go to Fujian to take office. As for the duties in Fujian Province, Chairman Jiang is currently responsible for them, so it is okay to arrive a little later. However, I must go to take office by the end of next month at the latest.

Leaving a Memorial 121

The January 28th Memorial Hall, which is being built here, is a memorial to the Songhu War of Resistance. Currently, everything is completed, except for a large mural, which will be completed soon. It was originally scheduled to open on August 1st, but due to the sudden urgency of time, it will probably be postponed to the 10th of next month.

Zhang Xiang Remains 122

The report that Fuzhou is about to be changed to a city and that Chief of Staff Zhang will be transferred to the mayor of Fuzhou is inaccurate. I have not heard of the rumors that Chairman Jiang will go to Guangdong after I arrive in Fujian. I met Minister Huang in Lushan and learned that Chief of Staff Deng Shizeng has the intention of coming north, but there is no definite news yet.

National Federation of Commerce Asks for Increased Tax on Foreign Rice 126

To Rescue the Declining Rural Economy

To Curb Dumping and Maintain the National Foundation

Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, in order to rescue the declining rural economy and maintain the national foundation, yesterday sent a special telegram to the central government requesting an increase in the import tax on foreign rice. The original telegram reads: "To the Nanjing National Government Executive Yuan Ministry of Foreign Affairs Ministry of Finance Ministry of Industry, Upon receiving a letter from the Zhangpu County Chamber of Commerce in Fujian, we found that Zhangpu was originally a rice-producing area, and the rural economy relied entirely on the export of rice to provide funding. However, this year, due to the impact of foreign rice dumping, not only has the export route been cut off, but the local market has also been occupied by foreign rice, resulting in the risk of spoilage. The rural economy is also on the verge of bankruptcy. If Zhangpu, a remote small county, has suffered so much, the impact on other rice-producing areas is self-evident. If no measures are taken to curb dumping, the future of our country's rural areas will be unimaginable. Therefore, we request that you investigate and forward this to the central government, and impose a heavy import tax on foreign rice to curb its dumping, in order to maintain the production of farmers across the country. This is truly a matter of public interest, etc. Upon approval of this, we find that the decline of our country's rural economy has various causes, but the drop in rice prices is the biggest key. The reason for the drop in rice prices is the impact of foreign rice dumping. Our country is based on agriculture, and agricultural products are sufficient for self-sufficiency. However, due to the squeezing of foreign rice dumping, the rural economy is in a state of bankruptcy. If no remedial measures are taken urgently, the danger is extremely great. The association, witnessing the difficulties of the times, requests that you immediately find a way to increase the import tax on rice to avoid surpluses and maintain the national foundation. This is our sincere plea. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, respectfully."

Postage to Nanyang Decided to be Increased Starting September 1st 130

But Overseas Chinese Still Vigorously Oppose

The Ministry of Communications originally planned to implement the Nanyang postage increase on May 1st. Ministry of Finance Collects Paper Money Tax 131

To be Collected from Banks Next Month

According to the Central News Agency, according to sources in the banking industry in this port, the Ministry of Finance, in order to increase national treasury revenue, has been collecting a 1.25% paper money tax since last year. The tax is stipulated to be collected once a year. The calculation method is for each bank to list the total number of banknotes issued every ten days and submit it to the Ministry of Finance for registration. It is calculated on an average basis at the end of each year and taxes are paid according to regulations. The Ministry of Finance has already started calculating the tax amount from July 1st last year to the end of June this year and will collect it from various banks at the beginning of next month, totaling about 3 million yuan. The total number of banknotes issued by various banks in this port last year is as follows: Bank of China more than 90 million yuan, Central Bank more than 45 million yuan, Bank of Communications more than 35 million yuan, the Four Banks more than 35 million yuan, Ningpo Commercial Bank more than 25 million yuan, China Industrial Bank more than 20 million yuan, Zhejiang Industrial Bank more than 7 million yuan, and Agricultural and Industrial Bank more than 2 million yuan, totaling more than 300 million yuan.

National Federation of Commerce Sends Telegram to Ministry of Finance Requesting Repeal of New Special Tax on Domestic Tobacco 132

The National Federation of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance yesterday to repeal the new special tax on domestic tobacco, stating: "To the Nanjing Ministry of Finance, Upon receiving a letter from the Jiujiang City Chamber of Commerce in Jiangxi, which states: "The Jiujiang Customs Transit Industry Association writes that the members of the association, including Li Hengmao, Gong Yuchang, Rishengdong, Yongda'an, Wanli, Wang Jinji, Hengshun, Shentai, Qianshengji, Ding Shen, Qingfeng, and other firms, state that our association has opened customs transit warehouses in Xun, relying on the tobacco leaf production in Ruijin, Guangchang, Poyang, Duchang, and Ruichang in Jiangxi, Suqian in Anhui, and Huangmei and Guangji in Hubei. Over the years, tobacco merchants have transported goods to Xun, and our association has acted as their customs broker and transit agent, and has also advanced customs duties and transportation fees. For small businesses, we have even had to provide them with loans to facilitate their turnover. Recently, due to sluggish business and tight finances, the tobacco leaves that have been pledged in Xun have not been transported for export because there is no money to repay the loans. However, these tobacco leaves all left the place of origin before the promulgation of the new regulations and have paid all the taxes and fees. Jiujiang is not a production area, so how can we force them to levy taxes again? Moreover, the new regulations were implemented on July 1st, and the tobacco leaves that have been in port for a long time are not within the scope of the new regulations. The law can still be lenient to the past, and we cannot make exceptional and harsh demands. In the past, the Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau was also an agency established by the Ministry of Finance. Since the new regulations have been changed and have not been promulgated, the tobacco leaves that have completed the payment of taxes cannot be sold. Is this reasonable? If the place of origin tax bill is issued after the implementation of the new regulations and the required tax rate has not been paid, it should be paid by the Local Tobacco Special Tax Bureau, which is proper, and tobacco merchants have no objection. Now, under the pretext of the new regulations, they are forcibly collecting taxes on tobacco leaves that are unrelated, which is a direct pain for tobacco merchants due to heavy taxes, and our association is indirectly affected by the depletion of business. Having no other choice, we have described the situation and request that your association forward it to the Jiujiang Local Tobacco Special Tax Bureau to release the stored tobacco leaves in accordance with the regulations, and not make things difficult for the sake of public order and to maintain commerce. It is also found that the Tax Administration has changed the tobacco and alcohol tax rates for this year, abolished the public sale, and issued new regulations with harsh clauses and heavy fines. Tobacco merchants everywhere are generally pessimistic, resulting in the stagnation of tobacco transportation, and our industry is becoming more and more deserted. However, Article 2 of the new regulations stipulates that each market scale of 100 catties will be levied 4 yuan and 1 jiao and 5 fen in national currency. The tobacco leaves produced in the above-mentioned eight counties of Ruijin and other counties are mostly of inferior quality, and the selling price is only 2 yuan to 4 yuan per 100 catties. Buyers are all tobacco shops, who sell silk for sale, and the smokers are also coolies and common people. Now, the tax rate is higher than the selling price, which is directly added to tobacco merchants and indirectly added to coolies. In recent years, disasters have occurred frequently, and the countryside has gone bankrupt. Tobacco merchants must seek other livelihoods in view of the future. As for the tobacco-producing areas, most of them are barren mountains and sandy soil, where grains cannot be grown. Their lifeline is entirely tied to tobacco leaves. If they cannot be sold, their livelihoods will be cut off. If the tens of millions of poor people are about to fill the ditches, our government cherishes the people's livelihood. Your association, representing the merchants, respectfully requests that you forward all the above-mentioned obstructive circumstances to the Ministry of Finance, and humbly request that you take back your orders and collect taxes as before, so as to increase national taxes and relieve the people's sentiments, etc. The public association forwarded the letter to the association. According to this, in addition to reporting the section on completed tax fees, which will be handled separately, it is found that the tax rate is higher than the selling price, which is what the country and the people cannot bear. According to the previous situation, it is reasonable to forward it to your association and ask you to check and treat the obstruction of the new chapter, transfer the report, etc. Upon approval, it is reasonable to send a telegram to your ministry, humbly requesting a review and approval, and humbly considering the livelihood of the poor people, take back the order, and still collect taxes according to the old chapter, and order the Jiujiang Local Tobacco Special Tax Bureau to quickly release the goods that have arrived in Xun before and have been taxed according to the old chapter, in order to relieve merchants from difficulties. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, respectfully."

Three People Rescued by the Hongxing Ship 134

Reported to All Parties in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

The Shanghai-Ningbo Hongxing ship departed from Ningbo at 4:35 p.m. on the 27th of this month (i.e., Thursday) and arrived in Shanghai. At about 12 o'clock that night, it sailed to the sea off Daji. At 12:25 a.m., it suddenly heard someone calling for help in the sea. The shipowner, Chuan Anxing, immediately stopped the ship to search. At that time, three people were rescued. Upon inquiry, it was learned that one was Fei Baozhong, 29 years old, who was the shipowner of the Jindeli ship; one was He Yongfu, 39 years old, who was the captain of the ship; and one was Tang Laichun, 19 years old, who was a partner of the ship. The Jindeli ship was carrying sand and mud from Qushan to Shanghai. At about 9:00 p.m. the night before, it sailed to the sea off Daji. Due to the adjustment of the wind gun, it was overturned by the wind. There were a total of nine people on the ship. Now, only three people have been rescued. The other six people cannot be found. They had no choice but to come to Shanghai at 1:15 a.m. yesterday. Now, the shipowner, Chuan Anxing, has reported the matter separately to the relevant authorities for investigation.

Ancient Artifacts of the Palace Museum Continued to be Inspected Yesterday 135

Leather Clothing Shows Signs of Dampness

Will Attempt to Expose to Sunlight

According to the Central News Agency, the ancient artifacts storage of the Palace Museum has been inspecting the items stored in the boxes for several days. The results show that there is no dampness or mold. The situation is very good. Yesterday, the Palace Museum Supervisory Committee continued to open the boxes for inspection in groups. A total of more than 50 boxes were inspected in the morning. The calligraphy, paintings, books, documents, and other items were still dry and free of mold. However, the boxes containing leather clothing showed signs of dampness, and it was feared that the valuable leather clothing would be damaged. They will attempt to expose it to sunlight. Yesterday afternoon, all groups stopped working and did not continue the inspection. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited a museum staff member yesterday afternoon. According to him, the Supervisory Committee will hold a meeting tomorrow (i.e., today) to discuss everything and decide on the issue of exposure to sunlight. Therefore, the inspection will not continue temporarily tomorrow. As for the expansion of the Supervisory Committee, it must wait for the Palace Museum Board of Directors to hold a meeting to decide. The meeting of the Board of Directors will have to be postponed until around August 20. Shanghai Municipal Council States Purpose of Crackdown on Rubber Factories 136

Taxpayers' Association Forwarded the Letter to the Industry Association

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Shanghai International Settlement sent a letter to the Rubber Products Industry Association yesterday to forward the reply from the Shanghai Municipal Council, stating: "Regarding the case of the Shanghai Municipal Council's notice to Hongda, Yiyuan, Dade, Tianxing, and other rubber products factories to relocate, we have received the following reply from the Council: "To the Rubber Industry Association regarding the letter of July 11, protesting against the implementation of the safety measures stipulated by the Council and requesting that the order be withdrawn, since the beginning of this year, there have been three incidents of carelessness in the rubber factories in the settlement. The first time was on February 21, when 81 workers died. The second time was on February 24, which occurred in one of the factories currently ordered to relocate. Fortunately, the fire occurred outside of working hours, otherwise the tragedy would have been far greater than the former, because there are 200 female workers in the factory, and the equipment of the Taiping Gate is completely inapplicable. The third time was on June 16. Fortunately, the dangerous part of the factory had been isolated, otherwise the casualties would have been inevitable. Because of the third incident of carelessness, the Council believes that this issue cannot be postponed any longer and issued an order on June 17 for the first time to all factories whose factory premises are unsuitable to stop work altogether. Your association believes that the Council can seek hygiene and safety without ordering the factories to relocate. The reason why the Council ordered the relocation of six factories is because, first, it is absolutely impossible to isolate the dangerous work areas in their current factory buildings, and second, the site cannot withstand heavy loads. The rubber factory is most likely to cause fire hazards, which is the refining of light oil, which is not in line with the facts. According to the explosion of rubber factories, there are two reasons: one is the use of naphtha, and the other is the debris in the calendering room. Among the five jobs in the factory, the amount of naphtha used may cause danger: one is the reconciliation of light oil, the second is the number of soaking light oil, the third is the reconciliation of cement, the fourth is the number of cloth cement, and the fifth is the rubber shoe pattern. Moreover, the air stored in the rubber vulcanizer contains explosive properties. If the electrical equipment in each factory ordered to be relocated emits sparks, it may cause an explosion throughout the factory at any time. As for the other 20 factories, they have not been ordered to relocate, because three of them only manufacture rubber products, which are less dangerous, and the remaining 17 have been shown improvement measures and have been asked to report the implementation time. The time limit set by the Council is never neglected. Even the hygiene and other safety equipment mentioned by your association will be gradually promoted according to their financial resources and time. The inspection of factories has been discussed with the municipal government in order to meet the wishes of the Chinese, in order to find a way that can be accepted by all parties. However, no matter what the outcome of the negotiations, the Council cannot abandon its responsibility for public safety related to buildings and factories within the settlement. According to the above, the Council has no other way but to promote this policy in order to protect the safety of citizens' lives and property. Correspondingly, I hereby inform you, and I hope you will check and take care of it. Sincerely, the Shanghai National Rubber Products Industry Association."

Therefore, as a creditor, it protested to the Soviet Russian Embassy in China and the Japanese Embassy, opposing the sale between Japan and Russia in the form of private transfer, and asked them to pay attention to the rights and interests of the creditor. Since the protests were sent separately, it is now learned that the Japanese Embassy has formally replied to the bank's liquidation office after receiving the protest, requesting that it be forwarded to the government for verification. The Russian Ambassador has been in Beijing for a long time, so he has not yet received a reply.

Ferry "Yangtze River" Collides with Floating Dock 138

Slightly Damaged

According to the Tzu Lin Pao, the Yangtze River ferry between Xiaguan and Pukou was shipped from the United Kingdom to Shanghai on April 17. Because the dock in Nanjing was not yet completed, it was temporarily berthed near Chenjiazhui in the Huangpu River. Yesterday (26th), it sailed to the Jiangnan Shipyard to be repainted. When it sailed near the Longmao Dock in Pudong, due to the strong wind and rapid tide, the ship only had a draft of five feet. The huge ship was shallow, and it was stimulated by the waves, causing the bow of the ship to collide with the floating dock. The hull was also slightly damaged. It was then towed to the Fanan Shipyard by a tugboat in the evening and will stay in the dock for about two months before sailing to Nanjing.

Dr. Jiang Kanghu's Speech on the Situation in Canada 139

Japanese People Publish Absurd Remarks in Canada

Jiang Repeatedly Spoke to Reprimand His Delusion

Dr. Jiang Kanghu, director of the Chinese Department of McGill University in Canada, gave a speech at the Bankers Club at the invitation of the International Issues Research Association at 5 pm the day before yesterday (27th). The following is a record of his speech (hereinafter, Jiang Jun's own words) Canada is north of the United States, with an area that is one-fifth larger than the United States, but its population accounts for only one-tenth of that of the United States. McGill University is located in Montreal, the capital of Kandong, and the city's population accounts for one-eighth of the country, which is also a strange thing. I have been in the United States and Canada for a total of eight years, and although I am engaged in the work of promoting Chinese culture, I can also say that I have a close relationship with international issues, because since the September 18th Incident, the tide of the Sino-Japanese issue has impacted the eyes and ears of the world. In order to understand the truth of the matter, people there often ask me to speak, averaging 70 to 80 times a year. However, in fact, it is quite difficult, because there is a lack of materials and talents. I have to interpret the newspapers. For example, the destruction of the Oriental Library Business Press has published declarations in the name of university professors, which were published in various newspapers. What is most hateful is that the Japanese people are very active in various places in the Americas and publish absurd remarks, such as referring to the 19th Route Army as a Red Army, and Manchuria is not Chinese territory. Its independence is the liberation of the nation, and for the sake of world peace, we have to protect Manchuria, and that a quarter of China's land has been completely occupied by the Red Army, and China has no ability to deal with this matter. Now that Manchuria has been established, the exchanges between China and Russia can be isolated from now on. This move is to directly help China to avoid the spread of the Red Army and indirectly seek world peace, etc. I have heard all these things with my own ears. As for the publications, there are already more than a dozen huge books published on the Manchurian side. There are two clubs in Montreal, Empire and Canadian, which are the most famous there (according to reports, Japan already has an embassy in Canada). They even asked the club to speak there, which shows how careful they are. Looking back at our government, it can be said that it has no work to promote abroad. Our country's propaganda there is only for a few students. In addition, there are incidental reports. Canada's immigration regulations have always been very strict. International students must have two years of university education to be admitted, and they are not allowed to work or practice there. Moreover, they must leave the country after graduation. Later, the director of the Immigration Bureau there asked me to review Chinese student affairs for the bureau, so I was able to dredge it up, and the conditions have been relaxed, that is, high school graduates can also go there, and they are allowed to work outside the school, but they must have at least ten credits per semester. After graduation, if they study science, they can also study in Canada without having to leave the country first. Those who want to study in Canada can contact me directly, etc. It is heard that Jiang Jun feels that the Chinese people are quite isolated from the situation in Canada, and plans to give more public speeches on a regular basis, focusing on Canada.

The Fish Association's Office Will Hold a Representative Conference Today 142

The Shanghai Office of the Jiangzhe Fish Industry Guild will convene a representative conference at 2 PM today. Representatives from Shaoxing and Wenjia (under Wuxing County) have already arrived and reported to the association yesterday. Representatives from Taizhou, Ningbo, Jiaxing, Huzhou, Wenzhou, Shipu (under Xiangshan County), Yuyao, Kunshan, and Zhenjiang are also en route to Shanghai, and are expected to arrive this morning. The conference agenda will include a report on the past disputes regarding fishery construction fees and the future policies to be adopted. Yesterday, the association also printed and distributed "The Opinions of the Third Mediator, with Original Text Attached," for distribution at the meeting. As it has not been previously published, it is transcribed below. Regarding the fishery construction fee case, after two rounds of mediation by He De and others, and after announcing the minister's sincerity in cooperating with the fishery industry to the representatives, the representatives were able to understand. However, they strongly criticized the misconduct of the collection personnel and the inadequate protection provided by the naval patrol ships. Regarding the construction fee itself, they also had several points that they insisted on requesting from the ministry. He De and others, after considering all opinions and adding their own suggestions, propose the following measures: 1. Shellfish are mostly sold in small quantities, and collecting fees seems excessively petty and the actual revenue is small, so it is proposed to exempt them. 2. Salted fish and seafood that have already paid customs duties should not be subject to construction fees again, as this is double taxation, so it is proposed to exempt them. 3. All frozen and salted fish that are subject to fees should be collected by the initial trading firm when they are first sold. For example, fish in barrels from Shenjiamen (under Dinghai County) should be collected by the fish firms in Shenjiamen. Once the fee is collected, it should not be collected again regardless of where the fish are transported. 4. To reduce collection costs and avoid harassment, it is proposed that the construction fee be determined separately by fish firms in various locations and remitted monthly. 5. Naval protection is of utmost importance and should be handled entirely by government authorities to avoid misunderstandings. It is proposed to establish a naval protection committee within the management bureau to allow merchant participation. Branch associations should also be established in Ningbo, Zhenhai, and Dinghai. The main duties include formulating naval protection plans and calculating naval protection expenses. 6. The existing various license fees and miscellaneous fees should be abolished by the ministry as soon as possible. 7. There is no need to establish a collection office. Previous funds (such as those for purchasing ships) should be returned by the ministry. The above items are only a general outline, and if they are adopted, the details will be discussed one by one for implementation.

Record of the Special Committee for Constitutional Research of the Lawyers Association 146

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened the first meeting of the Special Committee for Constitutional Research at 4 PM yesterday. The members present were Li Guozhen, Qiu Hanping, Hu Chongji, Wang Weizhen, Shen Junru, Li Mo, Li Mian, Ling Qihan, Tian Heming, Zhang Zhirang, etc. Zhang Zhirang was elected chairman, and Dai Jixian recorded the minutes. After the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, Wang Weizhen reported on the Lawyers Association's Constitutional Research Committee's recommendation that the Shanghai Lawyers Association study the General Provisions of the first compilation of the Constitution. The Executive and Supervisory Committee of the Association resolved that the constitution-making was a major national plan that could not be ignored. Therefore, all members present today were appointed to study the entire draft constitution and review the General Provisions of the first compilation. He asked everyone to express their great views and discuss them at length. Subsequently, Li Mian proposed that the period for studying the draft constitution was very short, and that holding meetings might not be possible within the allotted time. He proposed that each member submit their research opinions on the draft constitution in writing, which would save time and effort. Then, Tian Heming proposed organizing a sub-committee for review. After a long discussion, the following methods were decided: 1. Members of this committee should submit their research opinions on the entire or part of the draft constitution to the association by the 5th of this month for review, and a sub-committee meeting will be convened on August 8th to review the opinions, limited to eight days to complete the report and convene a general meeting of all committee members. 2. The number of members of the sub-committee is determined to be three. 3. Tian Heming, Ling Qihan, and Hu Chongji were appointed as members of the sub-committee, and Tian Heming was appointed as the person responsible for convening the meeting. 4. The committee meeting to be convened on August 9th is scheduled to be held at 6 PM. 5. Members of the Shanghai Lawyers Association should submit their opinions on the draft constitution to the association before August 5th for review, and a public announcement should be made to notify all members to take note. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

The Health Bureau Provides Free Vaccinations to Poor People in Western Shanghai 151

In the Caobao Road area of western Shanghai, cholera suddenly broke out a few days ago, and more than a dozen people have died due to lack of treatment, as reported in previous news. The district chief of the sixth district, Tan, concerned about the spread of the epidemic, sent a special letter to the Health Bureau requesting immediate remedial measures. Li, the director of the Health Bureau, first sent personnel to conduct an on-site investigation and found that it was chronic cholera and would not spread immediately. Therefore, there have been no further cases in recent days. In order to prevent and eliminate the disease, three doctors were dispatched from the 27th to administer preventive vaccinations in the Caobao Road and Jessfield Road areas. The poor residents generally welcomed and readily accepted the vaccinations, and a total of more than 1,700 people were vaccinated. It is said that because many poor people live in the area, vaccinations will need to continue for several days.

Record of the Yangzhou Fellow Association Meeting Regarding Zhu Shaotong's False Accusation 153

The Yangzhou Fellow Association held an executive committee meeting the day before yesterday, with 25 members present. Song Shixiang was elected chairman and the formalities were observed. Chen Qiannian reported that member Zhu Shaotong was employed at the Yifeng Porcelain Factory. On June 17th, he took leave to visit his relatives in Yangzhou. On the 28th, while passing by Hou'an Village, three thugs suddenly robbed Zhu of his watch and gown. (Shanghai slang: "peeling the pig's hide"). Zhu shouted and chased after them. When the thugs saw pedestrians, they knew they could not escape and instead grabbed Zhu, falsely claiming that they saw Zhu was the bandit who cut off the genitals of a child named Zheng. (At the time, there were rumors in Yangzhou about cutting off genitals.) When pedestrians heard this, they shouted and rushed forward, indiscriminately seizing Zhu and taking him to the local Public Security Bureau, falsely claiming that a child named Zheng had his genitals cut off. The bureau did not investigate and forced Zhu to confess under torture that he cut off the genitals of the child and sold them to a Shanghai pharmacy. Afterwards, the Zheng family went to the Public Security Bureau to declare that the child was safe at home and that nothing had happened. (Zheng also published a statement in the newspaper.) Then, Zhu was transferred to the county government, where he was still tortured and forced to confess to various unfounded facts. The president of the Chamber of Commerce, Wang Jingting, knowing this rumor, strongly defended Zhu to the county magistrate, like cutting paper figures with hairstyles, and secured Zhu's release on bail. Zhu suffered injuries and humiliation and went to the court to have his injuries examined, which is still under investigation. Zhu is 24 years old and has a legitimate job. The county magistrate did not prohibit the rumors in Yangzhou in advance, nor did he investigate the truth afterwards. Instead, he released the robbers who robbed Zhu and allowed them to falsely accuse an innocent civilian. He used torture to extract a confession. The association was requested to seek justice for its member. All members of the association were indignant upon hearing this and held an emergency meeting. They all believed that the county magistrate should maintain local order and stability, and should not listen to rumors and torture innocent civilians. They decided to send member Ruan Mubai to Yangzhou for a secret investigation, and appointed Song Shiyi to draft a petition to the provincial government and the Control Yuan, requesting that the county magistrate be severely punished according to the law. The meeting adjourned, and the clock struck six.
